C) Following the Hanafi madhhab, respecting scholars, and performing Hajj.
D) Belief in predestination, avoiding innovation, and loving the Prophet's family.

Key Takeaway
Anas ibn Malik defines Ahl al-Sunnah by love for Abu Bakr and Umar, respect for Uthman and Ali, and affirmation of wiping over khuffs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly love Abu Bakr and Umar in your heart, or do you merely acknowledge their status without any emotional attachment? In what ways does your life reflect that love—through defending their honor, following their example, or something else? Be honest: if your love were tested, would it hold?
?
Have you ever, even in a private moment or in jest, said something negative about Uthman or Ali? How does that align with Anas's second sign? If you have, what would it take for you to cut off that habit entirely and replace it with respect for all the Companions?
?
Anas includes a specific, practical sunnah—wiping over khuffs—as a defining feature of Ahl al-Sunnah. When you find that practice inconvenient, do you still do it out of obedience, or do you look for excuses to avoid it? What does your answer reveal about your commitment to being from the saved group?

The Batiniyya and the Meaning of Ilhad
Author defines the Batiniyya and the term ilhad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the error of the Batiniyya and the definition of ilhad as deviation from Islam that leads to disbelief.

Core Idea
Ilhad is the inward twisting of revelation to destroy the Sharia from within.

The author identifies a specific group that deviates from the apparent meanings of texts: the Batiniyya. He explains their claim that texts have hidden meanings known only to their teacher, and reveals their true purpose: to negate the Sharia entirely. Then he defines ilhad as a deviation from Islam that amounts to kufr because it denies what the Prophet brought. This lesson unpacks these critical definitions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the two parts: description of the Batiniyya and definition of ilhad.
2
Analyze the Batiniyya claim
Identify why they are called Batiniyya and what they claim about texts. What is their ultimate purpose?
Their purpose is to negate the Sharia entirely.
3
Understand the definition of ilhad
Break down the definition: inclination and deviation from Islam, connecting with kufr because it denies the Prophet in matters known necessarily.
Ilhad is not just heresy but a specific kind of deviation.
4
Connect to broader Aqeedah
Reflect on why this is harmful: it denies what is known necessarily from the Prophet, which is a fundamental breach.
This relates to the concept of daruriyyat ad-din.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالعدول عنها ) أى عن الظواهر ( إلى معان يدعيها أهل الباطن وهم الملاحدة - وسموا الباطنية - لادعائهم أن النصوص ليست على ظواهرها بل لها معان باطنة لا يعرفها إلا المعلم. وقصدهم بذلك : نفى الشريعة بالكلية. (إلحاد) أى ميل وعدول عن الإسلام واتصال واتصاف بكفر لكونه تكذيبا للنبي عليه السلام فيما علم مجيئه بالضرورة . وأما ما يذهب إليه بعض المحققين من أن النصوص محمولة على ظواهرها، ومع ذلك ففيها إشارات خفية إلى دقائق تنكشف على أرباب السلوك، يمكن التطبيق بينها وبين الظواهر المرادة، فهو من كمال الإيمان ومحض العرفان (۱) . (۱) كما في بعض التفاسير الصوفية .
So deviation from them—i.e., from the apparent meanings—to meanings claimed by the people of the inner, and they are the heretics – they were called al-Batiniyya – because of their claim that the texts are not upon their apparent meanings but rather they have inner meanings that no one knows except the teacher. Their purpose in that is to completely negate the Sharia. (Ilhad) means inclination and deviation from Islam, and connection and characterization with disbelief, because it is a denial of the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding what is known necessarily that he brought. And as for what some of the muhaqqiqun hold, that the texts are carried upon their apparent meanings, and yet they contain hidden allusions to subtleties that are disclosed to the people of spiritual wayfaring, and it is possible to reconcile between them and the intended apparent meanings, then that is from the perfection of faith and pure gnosis. (1) As in some Sufi commentaries.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage explains the errors of the Batiniyya (esotericists who claim texts have hidden meanings only known to their teacher) and defines ilhad as deviation from Islam leading to kufr because it entails denying the Prophet's message. It then distinguishes the sound approach of the muhaqqiqun (verifiers) who affirm apparent meanings while acknowledging deeper allusions (isharat) that do not contradict them, which is praiseworthy and considered perfection of faith. A footnote indicates that such allusions are found in some Sufi commentaries.

معلم
نفى الشريعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Batiniyya's inner meanings are a legitimate spiritual interpretation of texts.
Correction: The Batiniyya's claim rejects the apparent meanings and aims to undermine the Sharia, which is a form of ilhad (deviation) leading to disbelief.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of the Batiniyya in claiming inner meanings for texts?
A) To show the depth of the Quran.
B) To completely negate the Sharia.
C) To reconcile contradictions.
D) To follow the examples of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Batiniyya's esoteric reading of texts is a deliberate distortion aimed at destroying the Sharia, and such deviation is ilhad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life have you rationalized away clear Islamic rulings by claiming a 'deeper understanding' that only you or your group sees? What is the difference between seeking wisdom and distorting revelation?
?
The Batiniyya claimed that only their teacher knows the true meaning. Do you have any religious leader or scholar whose word you take as unquestionable, even when it contradicts the clear texts? How would you recognize if you are falling into blind following that leads to deviation?
?
Ilhad is defined as deviation from Islam by denying what the Prophet brought. In your daily life, are there any aspects of the Sunnah that you downplay or reinterpret because they are inconvenient? Is your hesitation a form of subtle ilhad?

The Correct Approach: Apparent Meanings and Inner Allusions
Author presents the correct approach of muhaqqiqun regarding texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct hermeneutical approach of the muhaqqiqun (verifiers) which affirms the apparent meanings of texts while acknowledging hidden allusions that can be reconciled.

Core Idea
True spiritual insight does not negate apparent meanings; it adds depth without contradiction.

After condemning the Batiniyya's dangerous esotericism, the author clarifies that there is a legitimate way to recognize deeper meanings in texts. The muhaqqiqun (verifiers) hold that texts are carried on their apparent meanings, yet they also contain hidden allusions (isharat) to subtleties that are disclosed to the people of spiritual wayfaring (arbab as-suluk). These allusions can be reconciled with the apparent meanings, and this approach is praised as perfection of faith and pure gnosis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the contrast with the previous lesson on the Batiniyya.
2
Identify the position of the muhaqqiqun
What do the muhaqqiqun hold about texts? They affirm the apparent meanings but also see hidden allusions.
3
Understand the concept of ishara
The allusions (isharat) are hidden subtleties disclosed to the people of spiritual wayfaring. They do not contradict the apparent meaning.
4
Appreciate the value
The author says this is from the perfection of faith and pure gnosis. Why is it praiseworthy?
Because it combines literal adherence with spiritual depth.

(إلحاد) أى ميل وعدول عن الإسلام واتصال واتصاف بكفر لكونه تكذيبا للنبي عليه السلام فيما علم مجيئه بالضرورة . وأما ما يذهب إليه بعض المحققين من أن النصوص محمولة على ظواهرها، ومع ذلك ففيها إشارات خفية إلى دقائق تنكشف على أرباب السلوك، يمكن التطبيق بينها وبين الظواهر المرادة، فهو من كمال الإيمان ومحض العرفان (۱) . (۱) كما في بعض التفاسير الصوفية .
So deviation from them—i.e., from the apparent meanings—to meanings claimed by the people of the inner, and they are the heretics – they were called al-Batiniyya – because of their claim that the texts are not upon their apparent meanings but rather they have inner meanings that no one knows except the teacher. Their purpose in that is to completely negate the Sharia. (Ilhad) means inclination and deviation from Islam, and connection and characterization with disbelief, because it is a denial of the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding what is known necessarily that he brought. And as for what some of the muhaqqiqun hold, that the texts are carried upon their apparent meanings, and yet they contain hidden allusions to subtleties that are disclosed to the people of spiritual wayfaring, and it is possible to reconcile between them and the intended apparent meanings, then that is from the perfection of faith and pure gnosis. (1) As in some Sufi commentaries.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage explains the errors of the Batiniyya (esotericists who claim texts have hidden meanings only known to their teacher) and defines ilhad as deviation from Islam leading to kufr because it entails denying the Prophet's message. It then distinguishes the sound approach of the muhaqqiqun (verifiers) who affirm apparent meanings while acknowledging deeper allusions (isharat) that do not contradict them, which is praiseworthy and considered perfection of faith. A footnote indicates that such allusions are found in some Sufi commentaries.

Key Terms
محققون
إشارات
أرباب السلوك
عرفان
ظواهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any interpretation beyond the apparent meaning is heretical.
Correction: The muhaqqiqun affirm that texts have both apparent meanings and hidden allusions, and reconciling them is a sign of perfect faith.

Checkpoint
According to the muhaqqiqun, what is the relationship between the apparent meanings of texts and the hidden allusions?
A) The hidden allusions are the only intended meaning.
B) The apparent meanings are false and must be ignored.
C) Texts are on their apparent meanings but also have reconcilable allusions.
D) The allusions are only known to the teacher.

Key Takeaway
The correct hermeneutic affirms the apparent meanings while recognizing deeper allusions, and harmonizing them is a sign of perfected faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Qur'an or hadith, do you stop at the surface meaning, or do you actively seek deeper allusions? How can you train yourself to look for both without forsaking the apparent?
?
The author says that reconciling apparent meanings with hidden allusions is 'from the perfection of faith.' Is your faith content with just one layer? What would change in your practice if you truly believed a text could hold both?
?
Are you among those who fear inner meanings because of the errors of the Batiniyya? What specific step can you take today to approach a verse with the mindset of a muḥaqqiq—affirming the obvious while remaining open to subtleties?

The Non-Existent is Not a Thing: Ontological Meaning
Explains the ontological meaning of 'the non-existent is not a thing' and the Mu'tazila dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the non-existent has no ontological status and how the verifiers (al-muhaqqiqun) refute the Mu'tazila claim that non-existent possibles are fixed externally.

Core Idea
The non-existent has no fixed reality; it is pure negation.

In this lesson, we explore the central kalam axiom that 'the non-existent is not a thing' in the sense of having no fixed existence. This position is defended by the verifiers against the Mu'tazila, who attribute a kind of fixedness to possible non-existents. Understanding this distinction is foundational for debates about divine attributes and creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author defines 'thing' as fixed and established.
The opening parenthesis is as in the original.
2
Identify key terms
Find the terms shay'iyya, wujud, thubut, 'adam, nafy. Understand their relationships.
These are synonyms in this context.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila opposition
The passage calls the judgment 'necessary' and notes that only the Mu'tazila dispute it. Ask why this is a key differentiator.
This dispute is a major point of Sunni-Mu'tazili divergence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعدوم ليس بشيء ) إن أريد بالشيء الثابت المتحقق على ما ذهب إليه المحققون من أن الشيئية ترادف الوجود والثبوت والعدم يرادف النفى . وهذا حكم ضرورى لم ينازع فيه إلا المعتزلة القائلون بأن المعدوم الممكن ثابت في الخارج. وإن أريد أن المعدوم لا يسمى شيئا، فهو بحث لغوى مبنى على تفسير الشيء : أنه الموجود أو المعدوم أو ما يصح أن يعلم أو يخبر عنه فالمرجع إلى النقل وتتبع موارد الاستعمال.
And the non-existent is not a thing. If by 'thing' is meant the fixed, the established, according to what the verifiers (al-muhaqqiqun) have gone to — that thingness (al-shay'iyya) is synonymous with existence (al-wujud) and fixedness (al-thubut), and non-existence (al-'adam) is synonymous with negation (al-nafy). And this is a necessary judgment (hukm daruri) which none has disputed except the Mu'tazila, who say that the non-existent possible (al-ma'dum al-mumkin) is fixed (thabit) in the external world. And if it is intended that the non-existent is not called a thing, then it is a linguistic investigation (bahth lughawi) built on the interpretation of 'thing': that it is the existent, or the non-existent, or what is correct to be known or spoken about. So the reference is to transmission (al-naql) and tracing the contexts of usage.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage presents a two-part analysis of the statement 'The non-existent is not a thing' (al-ma'dum laysa bi shay'). It first considers the intended meaning if 'thing' refers to something fixed and established (al-thabit al-mutahaqqiq). According to the verifiers (al-muhaqqiqun), 'thingness' (shay'iyya) is synonymous with existence (wujud) and fixedness (thubut), and non-existence ('adam) is synonymous with negation (nafy). Therefore, the non-existent cannot be a thing in this sense. This is described as a necessary judgment (hukm daruri) that no one disputes except the Mu'tazila, who claim that the non-existent possible (al-ma'dum al-mumkin) is fixed (thabit) in the external world. The second part then considers a purely linguistic interpretation: if the statement means that the non-existent is not called a 'thing', then it is a philological question depending on how 'thing' is defined — whether it means existent, non-existent, or anything that can be known or spoken about. In that case, the answer is to be sought from transmitted usage and linguistic convention.

Key Terms
معدوم
شيء
ثبوت
وجود
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila believe that non-existent possibles are 'things' in a fixed sense.
Correction: According to the verifiers, non-existent possibles cannot be fixed externally; they are pure negations.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between thingness (al-shay'iyya) and existence (al-wujud)?
A) They are opposites
B) They are synonymous
C) Thingness is a form of non-existence
D) Existence is a part of thingness

Key Takeaway
The non-existent has no fixed reality; thingness is synonymous with existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the non-existent (like your dreams for the future) as if they already have reality in your heart, forgetting that only what Allah has decreed exists truly exists? How can you submit your hopes to His will today?
?
The Mu'tazila granted a kind of reality to what does not exist. Where in your life do you give weight to fears, grudges, or fantasies that have no actual existence—and what would it look like to release them and live only in the truth?
?
If thingness is synonymous with existence, then only Allah has real, necessary existence. Does your daily preoccupation reflect that you truly believe this? What one change can you make today to orient your heart fully toward the Real?

The Non-Existent is Not a Thing: Linguistic Interpretation
Explains the linguistic analysis of whether the non-existent is called a thing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic dimension of the debate: whether the non-existent can be called a 'thing' depends on definition and usage.

Core Idea
Whether the non-existent is called a 'thing' is a linguistic question, not an ontological one.

While the first meaning of 'the non-existent is not a thing' is ontological, there is also a purely linguistic interpretation. If we ask whether the non-existent deserves the name 'thing', the answer depends on how we define the word. This lesson explores that semantic investigation and its reliance on transmitted usage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the shift from ontology to linguistics.
2
Examine the three possible definitions of 'thing'
The passage lists three interpretations: existent, non-existent, or anything knowable/speakable. Understand each.
This shows the flexibility of the word.
3
Consider the final reference to usage
The passage concludes that the answer comes from tracing actual linguistic usage. Why does this matter?
It shifts authority from reason to transmitted language.

Source Text

If by 'thing' is meant the fixed, the established, according to what the verifiers (al-muhaqqiqun) have gone to — that thingness (al-shay'iyya) is synonymous with existence (al-wujud) and fixedness (al-thubut), and non-existence (al-'adam) is synonymous with negation (al-nafy). This passage presents a two-part analysis of the statement 'The non-existent is not a thing' (al-ma'dum laysa bi shay'). Linguistically, whether the non-existent is a 'thing' depends on definition and usage, not on ontology.

?
If you have ever debated whether the non-existent is a thing, would you now admit that much of the disagreement may have been linguistic rather than substantive? How can you avoid wasting time on such semantic debates while still defending core truths?

First Objection: Angels as Pure Spirits
First objection and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection against human superiority based on angels being pure spirits and why the author dismisses it as based on philosophical rather than Islamic principles.

Core Idea
Angelic purity does not prove superiority; it only reflects a philosophical view.

The first objection raised by the Mu'tazila, philosophers, and some Ash'aris is that angels are superior to humans because they are pure spirits, free from evil and physical limitations. This argument, however, relies on philosophical assumptions rather than Islamic sources. Let's examine the objection and its concise refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage and translation to grasp the argument and its refutation.
Notice the brevity of the response.
2
Identify the underlying assumption
The objection assumes that freedom from matter and evil implies superiority. The author counters that this is based on philosophical principles, not Islamic ones.
3
Reflect on the method
The author uses a simple yet powerful critique: dismissing the premise as foreign to Islamic thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهبت المعتزلة والفلاسفة وبعض الأشاعرة إلى تفضيل الملائكة: وتمسكوا بوجوه : الأول : أن الملائكة أرواح مجردة كاملة بالفعل. مبرءات عن مبادئ الشرور والآفات كالشهوة والغضب، وعن ظلمات الهيولى . والصورة قوية على الأفعال العجيبة عالمة بالكوائن ماضيها وآتيها من غير غلط . والجواب : أن مينى ذلك على أصول الفلاسفة دون الأصول الإسلامية. الثاني: أن الأنبياء مع كونهم أفضل البشر، يتعلمون ويستفيدون منهم بدليل قوله تعالي : و علمه شديد القوى ) [ النجم : ٥] وقوله تعالى : نزل به الروح الأمين ﴾ [الشعراء: ۱۹۳] ولا شك أن المعلم أفضل من المتعلم. والجواب : أن التعلم من الله، والملائكة إنما هم المبلغون . الثالث : أنه قد اضطرد فى الكتاب والسنة تقديم ذكرهم على ذكر الأنبياء. وما ذلك إلا لتقدمهم في الشرف والرتبة . والجواب : أن ذلك لتقدمهم في الوجود، أو لأن وجودهم أخفى فالإيمان بهم أقوى وبالتقديم أولى. الرابع: قوله تعالى ولن يستنكف الْمَسِيحُ أَن يَكُونَ عَبْدا لله ولا الملائكة المقربون ﴾ [النساء : ۱۷۲] فإن أهل اللسان يفهمون من ذلك أفضلية الملائكة من عيسى - عليه السلام - إذ القياس فى مثله : الترقى من الأدنى إلى الأعلى . يقال : لا يستنكف من هذا الأمر الوزير ولا السلطان ولا يقال : السلطان ولا الوزير ثم لا قائل بالفضل بين عيسى - عليه السلام - وغيره من الأنبياء . والجواب : أن النصارى استعظموا المسيح، بحيث يرتفع من أن يكون عبدا من عباد الله، بل ينبغى أن يكون ابنا له - سبحانه - لأنه مجرد لا أب له . وكان قادرا على إبراء الأكمه والأبرص ويحيى الموتى بخلاف سائر عباد الله، من بنی آدم فرد عليهم بأنه لا يستنكف من ذلك المسيح، ولا من هو أعلى منه فى هذا المعنى، وهم الملائكة الذين
The Mu'tazila, philosophers, and some Ash'aris held the preference of angels. They clung to points: First: that angels are pure spirits, complete in actuality, free from principles of evils and afflictions like lust and anger, and from the darkness of matter. They are powerful for wondrous deeds, knowing of events past and future without error. The answer: that this is based on the principles of the philosophers, not Islamic principles. Second: that the prophets, despite being the best of humans, learn and benefit from them, evidenced by His statement 'He taught him intense strength' (Quran 53:5) and His statement 'The Trustworthy Spirit descended with it' (Quran 26:193). No doubt the teacher is better than the learner. The answer: that learning is from Allah, and the angels are only conveyers. Third: that it is consistent in the Book and the Sunna to mention them before mentioning the prophets. That is only due to their precedence in honor and rank. The answer: that this is due to their precedence in existence, or because their existence is more hidden, so faith in them is stronger, and by precedence they are more worthy. Fourth: His statement, 'The Messiah will never disdain to be a servant of Allah, nor will the angels brought near' (Quran 4:172). The speakers of Arabic understand from this the preference of angels over Jesus, peace be upon him, because the analogy in such cases is progression from lower to higher. It is said: The minister and the sultan do not disdain this matter; it is not said: the sultan and the minister. Then there is no one who says there is preference between Jesus, peace be upon him, and other prophets. The answer: that the Christians magnified the Messiah, to the point that he is exalted from being a servant of Allah's servants, but rather he should be a son to Him, glorified be He, because he is a pure spirit with no father. And he was able to heal the blind and leper and revive the dead, unlike other servants of Allah from the children of Adam. So He refuted them by saying that the Messiah does not disdain this, nor does anyone who is higher than him in this sense, and they are the angels who ...
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage presents four objections raised by the Mu'tazila, philosophers, and some Ash'aris arguing for the superiority of angels over humans, along with their responses. The first objection: Angels are pure spirits, free from evil and afflictions like lust and anger, and have perfect knowledge. The response: This relies on philosophical principles, not Islamic ones. The second objection: Prophets learn from angels, as the Quran says Gabriel taught the Prophet. Since the teacher is superior to the learner, angels are superior. The response: Learning is from Allah; angels are only conveyers. The third objection: The Quran and Sunna consistently mention angels before prophets, indicating their higher rank. The response: This is because angels existed before prophets, or because their existence is hidden, making faith in them stronger and precedence merited. The fourth objection: The verse (4:172) mentions angels after the Messiah in a context where the higher is typically mentioned later. The response: The Christians exaggerated the Messiah's status, but the point is that neither the Messiah nor the angels disdain servitude; the analogy is about the lowest not disdaining, not about superiority. The passage ends mid-response.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الفلاسفة
الأشاعرة
أرواح مجردة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels are superior because they are made of light/pure spirit.
Correction: This is a philosophical claim, not an Islamic proof.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the first objection?
A) Because angels are not actually pure spirits
B) Because it is based on philosophical principles, not Islamic ones
C) Because angels lack knowledge
D) Because the objection is too brief

Key Takeaway
The first objection is dismissed because it relies on philosophical, not Islamic, foundations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a religious argument that sounds logical and elegant, do you check whether its foundation is Islamic or philosophical? How can you protect yourself from being swayed by non-Islamic reasoning?
?
Have you ever been convinced by a claim about Islam simply because it seemed intellectually satisfying, without checking if it aligns with the sources? What was that claim, and how would you evaluate it now?
?
The objection in this lesson sounds sophisticated – pure spirits, free from matter, perfect knowledge. If you were in a debate, how would you respond using only Islamic principles? What does that reveal about where your trust lies – in human philosophy or divine revelation?

Second Objection: Prophets Learn from Angels
Second objection and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection that prophets learn from angels (so angels are superior) and the author's response that learning is from Allah, not the angels.

Core Idea
Angels are only conveyers; true knowledge comes from Allah.

The second objection argues that since prophets learn from angels (e.g., Gabriel teaching the Prophet), the teacher (angel) must be superior to the learner (prophet). But this overlooks that the ultimate source of knowledge is Allah, not the intermediary. Let's see the objection and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the argument.
The objection cites Quranic verses.
2
Analyze the response
The author clarifies that learning is from Allah directly; angels are mere conveyers, not the source.
This reframes the teacher-student relationship.
3
Consider the implication
If angels are only messengers, their role does not make them superior to the prophets they serve.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهبت المعتزلة والفلاسفة وبعض الأشاعرة إلى تفضيل الملائكة: وتمسكوا بوجوه : الأول : أن الملائكة أرواح مجردة كاملة بالفعل. مبرءات عن مبادئ الشرور والآفات كالشهوة والغضب، وعن ظلمات الهيولى . والصورة قوية على الأفعال العجيبة عالمة بالكوائن ماضيها وآتيها من غير غلط . والجواب : أن مينى ذلك على أصول الفلاسفة دون الأصول الإسلامية. الثاني: أن الأنبياء مع كونهم أفضل البشر، يتعلمون ويستفيدون منهم بدليل قوله تعالي : و علمه شديد القوى ) [ النجم : ٥] وقوله تعالى : نزل به الروح الأمين ﴾ [الشعراء: ۱۹۳] ولا شك أن المعلم أفضل من المتعلم. والجواب : أن التعلم من الله، والملائكة إنما هم المبلغون . الثالث : أنه قد اضطرد فى الكتاب والسنة تقديم ذكرهم على ذكر الأنبياء. وما ذلك إلا لتقدمهم في الشرف والرتبة . والجواب : أن ذلك لتقدمهم في الوجود، أو لأن وجودهم أخفى فالإيمان بهم أقوى وبالتقديم أولى. الرابع: قوله تعالى ولن يستنكف الْمَسِيحُ أَن يَكُونَ عَبْدا لله ولا الملائكة المقربون ﴾ [النساء : ۱۷۲] فإن أهل اللسان يفهمون من ذلك أفضلية الملائكة من عيسى - عليه السلام - إذ القياس فى مثله : الترقى من الأدنى إلى الأعلى . يقال : لا يستنكف من هذا الأمر الوزير ولا السلطان ولا يقال : السلطان ولا الوزير ثم لا قائل بالفضل بين عيسى - عليه السلام - وغيره من الأنبياء . والجواب : أن النصارى استعظموا المسيح، بحيث يرتفع من أن يكون عبدا من عباد الله، بل ينبغى أن يكون ابنا له - سبحانه - لأنه مجرد لا أب له . وكان قادرا على إبراء الأكمه والأبرص ويحيى الموتى بخلاف سائر عباد الله، من بنی آدم فرد عليهم بأنه لا يستنكف من ذلك المسيح، ولا من هو أعلى منه فى هذا المعنى، وهم الملائكة الذين
The Mu'tazila, philosophers, and some Ash'aris held the preference of angels. They clung to points: First: that angels are pure spirits, complete in actuality, free from principles of evils and afflictions like lust and anger, and from the darkness of matter. They are powerful for wondrous deeds, knowing of events past and future without error. The answer: that this is based on the principles of the philosophers, not Islamic principles. Second: that the prophets, despite being the best of humans, learn and benefit from them, evidenced by His statement 'He taught him intense strength' (Quran 53:5) and His statement 'The Trustworthy Spirit descended with it' (Quran 26:193). No doubt the teacher is better than the learner. The answer: that learning is from Allah, and the angels are only conveyers. Third: that it is consistent in the Book and the Sunna to mention them before mentioning the prophets. That is only due to their precedence in honor and rank. The answer: that this is due to their precedence in existence, or because their existence is more hidden, so faith in them is stronger, and by precedence they are more worthy. Fourth: His statement, 'The Messiah will never disdain to be a servant of Allah, nor will the angels brought near' (Quran 4:172). The speakers of Arabic understand from this the preference of angels over Jesus, peace be upon him, because the analogy in such cases is progression from lower to higher. It is said: The minister and the sultan do not disdain this matter; it is not said: the sultan and the minister. Then there is no one who says there is preference between Jesus, peace be upon him, and other prophets. The answer: that the Christians magnified the Messiah, to the point that he is exalted from being a servant of Allah's servants, but rather he should be a son to Him, glorified be He, because he is a pure spirit with no father. And he was able to heal the blind and leper and revive the dead, unlike other servants of Allah from the children of Adam. So He refuted them by saying that the Messiah does not disdain this, nor does anyone who is higher than him in this sense, and they are the angels who ...
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage presents four objections raised by the Mu'tazila, philosophers, and some Ash'aris arguing for the superiority of angels over humans, along with their responses. The first objection: Angels are pure spirits, free from evil and afflictions like lust and anger, and have perfect knowledge. The response: This relies on philosophical principles, not Islamic ones. The second objection: Prophets learn from angels, as the Quran says Gabriel taught the Prophet. Since the teacher is superior to the learner, angels are superior. The response: Learning is from Allah; angels are only conveyers. The third objection: The Quran and Sunna consistently mention angels before prophets, indicating their higher rank. The response: This is because angels existed before prophets, or because their existence is hidden, making faith in them stronger and precedence merited. The fourth objection: The verse (4:172) mentions angels after the Messiah in a context where the higher is typically mentioned later. The response: The Christians exaggerated the Messiah's status, but the point is that neither the Messiah nor the angels disdain servitude; the analogy is about the lowest not disdaining, not about superiority. The passage ends mid-response.

Key Terms
مبلغون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to the second objection?
A) By denying that prophets learn
B) By stating that learning is from Allah and angels are merely conveyers
C) By claiming angels are not teachers
D) By citing a different verse

Key Takeaway
Angels are mere conveyers of divine knowledge, not the source, so their role does not imply superiority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you receive knowledge or guidance from a teacher, scholar, or book, do you consciously thank Allah as the true source, or do you inadvertently elevate the vessel to a position that belongs only to Allah?
?
The objectors assumed the teacher is necessarily superior. Is there anyone in your life—a mentor, parent, or leader—whom you have unknowingly placed above Allah in your heart as the ultimate authority? How can you realign your gratitude and dependence?
?
If even prophets learned only from Allah, how much more should you humble yourself when seeking knowledge? What is one practical step you can take today to acknowledge that every insight you gain is a direct gift from Allah?

Third Objection: Consistent Precedence in Scripture
Third objection and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third objection that angels are consistently mentioned before prophets in the Quran and Sunna, indicating higher rank, and the author's two possible counterarguments.

Core Idea
Mentioning angels first is about precedence in existence or hiddenness, not superiority.

The third objection points to a consistent pattern in the Quran and Sunna: angels are mentioned before prophets. The objectors argue this shows their higher rank. The author provides two possible explanations: either angels existed first, or their hidden nature requires stronger faith, justifying the order. Let's examine this.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the passage to see the argument and the two-part response.
2
Identify the two responses
The author gives two options: precedence in existence or precedence due to hiddenness of their existence.
3
Evaluate the logic
Both explanations show that order of mention does not necessarily imply superiority.

Source Text

Fourth Objection: Quranic Analogy (4:172)
Fourth objection and its incomplete refutation

Learning Objective

Core Idea
The verse's progression is about not disdaining servitude, not about ranking.

The fourth objection uses a linguistic argument from Quran 4:172, where the phrase 'The Messiah will never disdain to be a servant of Allah, nor will the angels brought near' is understood to present a progression from lower to higher, implying angels are higher than Jesus. The author begins a response focusing on Christian overestimation of Jesus, but the text breaks off. Let's examine what we have.

Do Prophets Learn from Angels?
Objection and answer: prophets learn from angels vs. learning is from Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection regarding prophets learning from angels and the answer that true teaching is from Allah alone.

Core Idea
Teachers are superior unless teaching is merely delivery.

In this lesson, we encounter a second argument against the superiority of prophets over angels. The objector claims that since prophets learn from angels (as in the Quran), the teacher must be higher. Let us examine the objection and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: first the objection, then the answer.
The objection cites two Quranic verses. The answer is brief.
2
Understand the objector's logic
The objector assumes that if A learns from B, then B is superior. This is based on a general principle that the teacher is better than the student.
3
Analyze the answer's refutation
The answer distinguishes between the true source of knowledge and the conveyor. Allah is the ultimate teacher; angels are only messengers.
This refutes the assumption by showing that the angel does not teach from itself.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this answer preserves the superiority of prophets while allowing them to receive revelation through angels.
This connects to the broader debate on the relative merits of prophets and angels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: أن الأنبياء مع كونهم أفضل البشر، يتعلمون ويستفيدون منهم بدليل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَلَّمَهُ شَدِيدُ الْقُوَىٰ﴾ [النجم: ٥] وقوله تعالى: ﴿نَزَلَ بِهِ الرُّوحُ الْأَمِينُ﴾ [الشعراء: ١٩٣] ولا شك أن المعلم أفضل من المتعلم.
والجواب: أن التعلم من الله، والملائكة إنما هم المبلغون.
The second: That the prophets, despite being the best of humans, learn and benefit from them (the angels) as evidenced by His statement the Exalted: 'And taught him the One of Mighty Powers' [53:5] and His statement the Exalted: 'The Trustworthy Spirit descended with it' [26:193]. There is no doubt that the teacher is better than the student. The answer: That learning is from God, and the angels are merely conveyors.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer pair. The objector argues that since prophets learn from angels (as seen in the Quran where Jibril teaches), the teacher is superior. The answer refutes this: the real teacher is Allah; angels are only messengers. Thus the objection does not prove angelic superiority.

?

Objection: Angels Mentioned Before Prophets
Objection and answer about textual order of angels and prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the consistent mention of angels before prophets in the Quran and Sunnah does not prove their superiority over prophets in rank.

Core Idea
Textual order does not always indicate rank; it can reflect existence or strength of faith.

The third objection argues that since the Quran and Sunnah consistently mention angels before prophets, angels must be superior. The author provides a twofold answer: first, the precedence may be due to temporal existence, and second, it may be to highlight the strength of faith required for belief in the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection carefully. Note that it claims consistency in the Book and Sunnah in mentioning angels before prophets.
This objection is based on a textual pattern.
2
Understand the reasoning
The objection infers from this textual pattern that angels have precedence in honor and rank. Reflect on why someone might think so.
3
Read the answer
Now read the author's answer. It offers two possible explanations: precedence in existence or hiddenness of existence.
The answer shows that textual order can have multiple reasons.
4
Reflect on the explanations
Consider how each explanation works: angels were created before humans, and they are unseen, making faith in them stronger.
5
Apply the principle
Generalize: textual order in scripture does not always indicate rank. Other factors can determine order.
This principle helps avoid misinterpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : أنه قد اضطرد فى الكتاب والسنة تقديم ذكرهم على ذكر الأنبياء. وما ذلك إلا لتقدمهم في الشرف والرتبة . والجواب : أن ذلك لتقدمهم في الوجود، أو لأن وجودهم أخفى : فالإيمان بهم أقوى وبالتقديم أولى.
The third: That it is consistently established in the Book and Sunnah to mention them (the angels) before mentioning the prophets. And that is only due to their precedence in honor and rank. The answer: That is due to their precedence in existence, or because their existence is more hidden, thus faith in them is stronger, and with precedence it is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is another objection-and-answer. The objector points out that angels are always mentioned before prophets in the Quran and hadith, implying their higher rank. The answer gives two possible explanations: (1) angels were created before humans, so they exist first, or (2) because they are unseen, believing in them requires stronger faith, so they are given priority in mention to emphasize that. Thus, the order does not prove superiority.

Key Terms
الكتاب والسنة
تقديم
الوجود
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The order of mention in scripture always indicates superiority in rank.
Correction: The order can be based on other factors like temporal existence or the strength of faith required, as shown in the author's answer.

Checkpoint
What is one reason given in the answer for why angels are mentioned before prophets?
A) Angels are more beautiful
B) Angels have more knowledge
C) Angels existed first
D) Prophets are later in time

Key Takeaway
The consistent mention of angels before prophets in scripture does not prove their superior rank; it can be explained by their prior creation or the hiddenness of their existence requiring stronger faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read an argument that seems obvious from the surface, like 'order in text means order in rank', are you quick to accept it, or do you pause to consider alternative explanations? How can this lesson train you to think more deeply about what you read?
?
The angels are hidden, yet faith in them is considered stronger because it requires belief without seeing. How strong is your own faith in the unseen aspects of your religion—such as angels, the afterlife, or the wisdom of Allah's commands? Is your faith in what is visible and tangible stronger? What step can you take today to increase your faith in the hidden realities?
?
If you were to apply the principle that 'order does not always imply rank' to your own life, where might you be mistaking precedence in your time or attention for real importance? For example, do you prioritize visible duties over hidden spiritual growth? What change can you commit to in response to this lesson?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
The Objection from Quran 4:172 and Its Answer
The author presents the fourth objection from Quran 4:172 and the answer explaining the verse's context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse about the Messiah and angels is used as an objection against the superiority of angels over Jesus, and how the context refutes that inference.

Core Idea
The order of mention does not prove superiority when the context is refuting exaggerated claims.

This lesson examines the fourth objection raised against the Ash'ari position that angels are superior to prophets. The objector cites Quran 4:172, where Jesus and angels are mentioned together, and argues from Arabic linguistic convention that the lower is mentioned first. The answer, however, reveals the verse's context: it refutes Christian claims of Jesus' divinity, and the 'progression' refers to specific qualities, not absolute honor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and the answer
Read the passage to see how the objector uses the verse and how the answer responds. Notice the structure: first the objection, then the answer.
2
Understand the linguistic argument
The objector claims that in Arabic, when two items are mentioned in a negative construction, the lower is mentioned first (e.g., 'the minister nor the king'). So mentioning Jesus before angels implies angels are higher.
This is called 'progressing from lower to higher' (الترقى من الأدنى إلى الأعلى).
3
Examine the answer's contextual explanation
The answer explains that the verse was revealed to refute Christians who magnified Jesus. The 'progression' refers to freedom from physical parents and ability to perform mighty acts, not absolute honor.
Angels are mentioned second because they are even more detached from physical origins (no parents) and can do greater miracles.
4
Reflect on the implication
Understand why this argument does not prove angels are superior to Jesus or prophets. The verse's purpose and the specific meaning of progression prevent that inference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: قوله تعالى ﴿وَلَنْ يَسْتَنْكِفَ الْمَسِيحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ عَبْدًا لِلَّهِ وَلَا الْمَلَائِكَةُ الْمُقَرَّبُونَ﴾ [النساء: 172] فإن أهل اللسان يفهمون من ذلك أفضلية الملائكة من عيسى عليه السلام إذ القياس في مثله: الترقى من الأدنى إلى الأعلى. يقال: لا يستنكف من هذا الأمر الوزير ولا السلطان ولا يقال: السلطان ولا الوزير. ثم لا قائل بالفضل بين عيسى عليه السلام وغيره من الأنبياء. والجواب: أن النصارى استعظموا المسيح بحيث يرتفع من أن يكون عبدًا من عباد الله، بل ينبغي أن يكون ابنًا له سبحانه لأنه مجرد لا أب له. وكان قادرًا على إبراء الأكمه والأبرص ويحيي الموتى بخلاف سائر عباد الله من بني آدم. فرد عليهم بأنه لا يستنكف من ذلك المسيح، ولا من هو أعلى منه في هذا المعنى، وهم الملائكة الذين لا أب لهم ولا أم. ويقدرون بإذن الله تعالى على أفعال أقوى وأعجب من إبراء الأكمه والأبرص وإحياء الموتى. فالترقى والعلو إنما هو في أمر التجرد وإظهار الآثار القوية لا في مطلق الشرف والكمال. فلا دلالة على أفضلية الملائكة.
The fourth: His statement the Exalted: 'And the Messiah will not disdain to be a servant of Allah, nor the angels brought near' [4:172]. For the people of language understand from that the superiority of angels over Jesus, peace be upon him, because the analogy in such a case is progression from lower to higher. It is said: 'the minister does not disdain this matter, nor the king,' but it is not said: 'the king nor the minister.' Then no one claims superiority between Jesus, peace be upon him, and other prophets. The answer: That the Christians magnified the Messiah, to the extent that he is raised above being a servant of Allah, rather he should be a son of Him - exalted is He - because he is pure (without father). And he was able to heal the blind and leprous and revive the dead unlike other servants of Allah from the sons of Adam. So He replied to them that the Messiah does not disdain that, nor those who are higher than him in this sense, and they are the angels who have no father or mother. And they are able, by Allah's permission, the Exalted, to perform acts stronger and more wondrous than healing the blind and leprous and reviving the dead. So the progression and elevation is only in the matter of being free from physical origin and manifestation of powerful effects, not in absolute honor and perfection. So there is no indication of the superiority of angels.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage contains the fourth objection and its answer. The objector uses the verse where both Jesus and angels are mentioned in a negative construction, arguing that Arabic usage places the lower item first. Since Jesus is mentioned first, angels are considered higher. The answer explains the context: the verse was revealed to refute Christian claims that Jesus is divine. The verse emphasizes that even Jesus, who has unique qualities (no father, miracles), does not disdain servitude to God, and neither do the angels, who are even more detached from physical origins (no parents) and capable of greater miracles. Thus, the 'progression' is about these specific qualities, not absolute honor. Hence, the verse does not prove angels are superior in every respect.

Key Terms
المسيح
الملائكة المقربون
الترقى
التجرد
الآثار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because Jesus is mentioned before angels in Quran 4:172, angels are absolutely superior to Jesus and all prophets.
Correction: The verse's order does not indicate absolute superiority; it reflects the context of refuting Christian claims. The 'progression' refers to specific qualities like freedom from physical parents and ability to perform mighty acts, not overall honor.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what does the progression in the verse 'the Messiah... nor the angels' indicate?
A) Angels are absolutely superior to Jesus
B) Jesus is superior to angels
C) The progression is in terms of being free from physical origin and mighty acts
D) The verse is about sinlessness

Key Takeaway
The verse's order does not imply superiority because the context is about refuting Christian exaggeration and the progression refers to freedom from physical parents and ability to perform mighty acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you ever assume that the order of words always indicates a hierarchy? How might this lesson challenge that assumption? What concrete step will you take to ensure you interpret verses with their full context?
?
The Christians exaggerated Jesus' status because of his miraculous birth and deeds. Are there any people in your life—scholars, leaders, or loved ones—whom you are tempted to elevate beyond their rightful, servant status before Allah? How does this verse call you to correct that tendency?
?
The answer in this verse hinges on a subtle distinction in meaning. How often do you content yourself with a surface-level understanding of Quranic verses rather than digging deeper? What will you sacrifice today to study the Quran with more depth and humility?
